  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_496db02b-0f83-493e-b48c-23d37e3fcd58'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer18413595644193113743">Legend states that there exists a mighty sword that makes its possessor invincible to his enemies. But there is a curse on anyone who lifts the sword for conquest. King Kareed of Archeld goes after this sword anyway, winning it from the King of Bellandra.   <span id="freeText18413595644193113743" style="display:none">Legend states that there exists a mighty sword that makes its possessor invincible to his enemies. But there is a curse on anyone who lifts the sword for conquest. King Kareed of Archeld goes after this sword anyway, winning it from the King of Bellandra. When he returns home from battle, he brings his daughter, Princess Torina, two special gifts. One is a unique crystal, in which she can view visions of the future. The other gift is the defeated king’s son Landen, who is to be her slave. Torina immediately releases Landen, who becomes a member of the King’s army and her close friend.<br /><br />But trouble is lurking in the kingdom of Archeld and people are accusing Landen of plotting against the King. Torina refuses to believe he would hurt her family. Then Torina begins seeing deadly visions in her crystal. Can she save her father’s life and the future of her kingdom?</span>
  <a data-text-id="18413595644193113743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/1492445-how-old-is-vesputo">How old is Vesputo?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1492445'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F420415.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/28526280-kara"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1592737601i/28526280._UY100_CR12,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28526280-kara">Kara</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
Vesputo is near thirty by the time Torina is 15, if I remember correctly. So at the start of the book, he is perhaps early to mid-twenties.
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_483394068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483394068" />
    <a title="Elsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15708587-elsa"><img alt="Elsa" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483394068?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elsa" href="/user/show/15708587-elsa">Elsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483394068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16614968039800979772">This book was one of my favorite books as a young adult. I loved the everything about it, the storyline, the writing, the characters, the prose. I remember poring over the pages, even to the point where I memorized a few passages. Not being a person who tends to read books or watch movies over again, I remember reading this book at least a good five times in my life. I even found this in audio format after I grew up, and listened to it again. <br/><br/>Everything about the story was so perfect and full of</span>
  <span id="freeText16614968039800979772" style="display:none">This book was one of my favorite books as a young adult. I loved the everything about it, the storyline, the writing, the characters, the prose. I remember poring over the pages, even to the point where I memorized a few passages. Not being a person who tends to read books or watch movies over again, I remember reading this book at least a good five times in my life. I even found this in audio format after I grew up, and listened to it again. <br /><br />Everything about the story was so perfect and full of imagination. The mental images I retained from reading the book stuck in my mind for many years. The story of Torina and Landen was so compelling and so real that it was easy feel the wonder of their childhood friendship, the confusion of their young adult years, and then the heartbreak of their life apart as they grew into the people that they would become. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Their reconciliation at the end was so well thought out and so beautifully done that I dropped tears as I read it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The book read like a real fairy tale with scenes reminiscent of the matches of ancient Roman gladiators, to the solid stone castle of English lords, to frigid mountain ranges like the pyranees. The plot never bored me and the story never grew old. And the characters were created with such love, that one could feel what they were feeling and sense their love, disappointment, frustration, or exultation. <br /><br />One of the best books of my childhood memories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16614968039800979772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer153070877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7939616449441629466">All right, I won't lie: I honestly have no idea how "good" this book is. This, to me, is pure nostalgia, with a dtwist of soul-food. Every time I read it again (frequent) attempting to determine the book's true "quality", I'm swept away by waves of love. Given the other ratings it's garnered, I suppose it must actually be well written. I'm glad, but I don't really care. This was the very first book of a significant length I read and was the first 'real' I'd ever owned (I think it was a prize fro</span>
  <span id="freeText7939616449441629466" style="display:none">All right, I won't lie: I honestly have no idea how "good" this book is. This, to me, is pure nostalgia, with a dtwist of soul-food. Every time I read it again (frequent) attempting to determine the book's true "quality", I'm swept away by waves of love. Given the other ratings it's garnered, I suppose it must actually be well written. I'm glad, but I don't really care. This was the very first book of a significant length I read and was the first 'real' I'd ever owned (I think it was a prize from the library?) and I devoured it. Any cliches or shallow characters are invisible to me now. It was my first, what can I say? Honestly, if I had to choose an all-time favorite book (please don't make me) I'd probably say this one, just because it launched me into a lifetime of reading. So thank you, Ms. Hanley. You're awesome.</span>

He gives Landen to Torina as a slave, but Torina frees him. Torina witnesses the murder of her father and has to run away to save her life.   <span id="freeText8505526497222124875" style="display:none">King Kareed conquers Bellandra and brings his daughter, Torina, two prizes from the war: a crystal ball and the son of the conquered king, Landen.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144237617" />
    <a title="Tammie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie"><img alt="Tammie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604938056p2/3506989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144237617?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammie" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie">Tammie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=trilogy">trilogy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=owned-mass-market-paper-back">owned-mass-market-paper-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=companion-series">companion-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=series-completed">series-completed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144237617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2329175940981989569">The Seer and the Sword is one of my favorite YA fantasies. I enjoyed reading the way the two characters fell in love. It was one of those stories that could be romantic without all of the kissing. <br/><br/>I've never been a huge fan of the love at first sight type romances that are so prevalent in books. Although they can be fun to read (and I've read my fair share), they generally seem to lack some substance. In this story we get to see and understand how and why they love each other, and it happens ove</span>
  <span id="freeText2329175940981989569" style="display:none">The Seer and the Sword is one of my favorite YA fantasies. I enjoyed reading the way the two characters fell in love. It was one of those stories that could be romantic without all of the kissing. <br /><br />I've never been a huge fan of the love at first sight type romances that are so prevalent in books. Although they can be fun to read (and I've read my fair share), they generally seem to lack some substance. In this story we get to see and understand how and why they love each other, and it happens over a span of several years. I think the growth of characters is what I love so much about this book.<br /><br />I do wish that some things had been filled in that were left out. There are some periods of time that are skipped over and I could have done with more scenes with Torina and Landen together, but I think it’s amazing how the author is able to convey their love for each other to the reader without a lot of that.<br /><br />It’s been several years since I’ve read this and because I loved it so much (and enjoyed the two companion books as well), every now and then I will check and see if Victoria Hanley has written anything new. So far there are only a couple of fairy books. I’m not all that interested in reading the fairy books, but I dearly wish she would write another fantasy like this one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2329175940981989569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_265738389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265738389" />
    <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile"><img alt="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546974316p2/7494844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265738389?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile">laurel [the suspected bibliophile]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780823415328" href="/book/show/1443570.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265738389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13570790333219961782">When King Kareed of Archeld invades the peaceful city of Bellandra and takes home its prince as his prisoner, he unwittingly sets off a chain reaction of events that will ripple through the years, leaving his daughter, Torina, and the Bellandran prince caught in the cross-hairs.<br/><br/>Deception. Politics. Trickery. Honor. And Love.<br/><br/>Oh my!<br/><br/>This is an old favorite. I've resisted rereading it for years because I wasn't sure how well it would hold up, particularly against the wave of phenomenal MG and YA fan</span>
  <span id="freeText13570790333219961782" style="display:none">When King Kareed of Archeld invades the peaceful city of Bellandra and takes home its prince as his prisoner, he unwittingly sets off a chain reaction of events that will ripple through the years, leaving his daughter, Torina, and the Bellandran prince caught in the cross-hairs.<br /><br />Deception. Politics. Trickery. Honor. And Love.<br /><br />Oh my!<br /><br />This is an old favorite. I've resisted rereading it for years because I wasn't sure how well it would hold up, particularly against the wave of phenomenal MG and YA fantasy books out there.<br /><br />To be fair, the writing is clunky, stilted and simplistic. The plotline is super fast, with years passing in a sentence and <i>a lot happening</i>. Seriously. A shit ton happens in this book—most of it rapidly unfolding in the last half. There are plot holes galore. There's little diversity. There's some super creepy icky romance shit between an almost thirty-year-old and a fifteen-year-old <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Double ick when he says he's loved her since she was twelve! Stranger danger, Torina! Stranger danger! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And yet.<br /><br />The magic of this book once again swept me off my feet. I was pulled into this magical world as the writing—sparse and simplistic as it is—portrayed entire countries and palaces and mountains in a few words that take some authors paragraphs.<br /><br />It reminds me of the wonders of old school high fantasy without any of the downfalls, where good battles evil and evil is a clever and handsome creepy dude.<br /><br />I still love the twisty turny nature of the plot, the evilness of Vesputo (if you think he's far-fetched in what he gets away with, lemme just let you take a peek at this month's newspaper), how many little clues and series of events and characters weave together to tell the story of an arrogant princess and a former prince—as they grow, change, are forced apart, and find each other once again.<br /><br />And I love the cover, drawn by my absolute favorite children's artist of all time, Trina Schart Hyman.<br /><br />It's childhood nostalgia in all its best forms.<br /><br />I wish more people knew about and loved this book as much as I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13570790333219961782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189861969" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4457241954686960528">Nothing new. A hero; a fiery, spirited princess (with red hair too, how original); a mythical sword (that is never actually <i>used</i>); a totally evil villain plotting to be king; a pseudo-Medieval European setting; the only thing sort-of fresh was the fact that the princess had a crystal ball that showed her the future. And even <i>that's</i> been done before.<br/><br/>There's nothing wrong with being derivative. I mean, look at Harry Potter. The ultimate example: a trio of friends with the main hero; the old, wise </span>
  <span id="freeText4457241954686960528" style="display:none">Nothing new. A hero; a fiery, spirited princess (with red hair too, how original); a mythical sword (that is never actually <i>used</i>); a totally evil villain plotting to be king; a pseudo-Medieval European setting; the only thing sort-of fresh was the fact that the princess had a crystal ball that showed her the future. And even <i>that's</i> been done before.<br /><br />There's nothing wrong with being derivative. I mean, look at Harry Potter. The ultimate example: a trio of friends with the main hero; the old, wise man; the absolutely evil source of all evil; classic wizard and magical creature lore. But somehow, HP doesn't feel the least bit cliched.<br /><br />The difference between JK Rowling and Victoria Hanley is that Rowling manages to see past the stereotypes and show us the human characters in their own right. In Hanley's work, I never get to see the characters or the plot elements as anything other than elements. <br /><br />That being said: it is somewhat of a good story...If you've never read any fantasy before.</span>

<div id="review_84433020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84433020" />
    <a title="Chocolategoddess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3139347-chocolategoddess"><img alt="Chocolategoddess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411846142p2/3139347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84433020?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chocolategoddess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chocolategoddess" href="/user/show/3139347-chocolategoddess">Chocolategoddess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552552707" href="/book/show/690085.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3139347-chocolategoddess?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3139347-chocolategoddess?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84433020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8255683004096682571">This was recommended to me a very long time ago by someone who'd read a little of my second novel and said I might like this.<br/><br/>A very long time ago, I may have liked this. I certainly see it was likened it to my second novel. The difficulty is, all the parts that are similar are parts I cut in the epic rewriting of that second novel.<br/><br/>Essentially, this book is your standard kid's fantasy adventure novel. It's very, very standard. Most of the characters have only one note (evil, innocent, stoic, wise</span>
  <span id="freeText8255683004096682571" style="display:none">This was recommended to me a very long time ago by someone who'd read a little of my second novel and said I might like this.<br /><br />A very long time ago, I may have liked this. I certainly see it was likened it to my second novel. The difficulty is, all the parts that are similar are parts I cut in the epic rewriting of that second novel.<br /><br />Essentially, this book is your standard kid's fantasy adventure novel. It's very, very standard. Most of the characters have only one note (evil, innocent, stoic, wise, kind etc) and they play up to those notes perfectly. There's a reasonable amount of political talk, but it's all simplistic and the reader is fully aware of who's going to back-stab whom. The plot line itself is predictable and feels vaguely familiar.<br /><br />The characters didn't particularly stand out for me. Many of them just kind of accepted horrible things happening to them, and only later would they fight. They also didn't question anything, which made my eyes roll repeatedly. I guess that's at the heart of my apathy for this story. The events just felt like pre-ordained things happening to people (even when the seer was changing the future, it was clear she was meant to change it). I never felt like these characters were more than just cardboard puppets being danced around.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Something that drove me up the wall was when Torina sees her father being murdered in her crystal ball, and runs to go warn him. But instead of shouting VESPUTO'S GOING TO KILL YOU so he could, y'know, arm himself, she faffs around trying to explain how she knows what she's about to tell him, so he's totally clueless and then Torina witnesses him being murdered. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The setting was very standard too. Classic stories like this can be dramatically improved by a bit of imagination in the setting, the magic, the creatures. This is pretty much just standard "medieval" fantasy, with no interesting creatures, and only the vaguest hint of magic in the form of a crystal ball that shows the future when it's plot-convenient, and a sword that apparently makes the wielder indestructible unless they're using it for conquest. The crystal ball gets a lot of play but little explanation, and the sword just kind of acts like a magical thingamabob that everyone wants. No one ever uses its power.<br /><br />The writing is what I consider a very basic style. There isn't a great deal of description, still less done in an interesting way. The feelings of the characters are "told" to us quite a lot. The point of view is third person omniscient and zooms around lots of characters. We don't benefit from the coloured perspective you get with third person limited, so it's all rather impersonal. I definitely felt like I was being told a story, rather than witnessing it.<br /><br />I can't get too annoyed about books like this, but sometimes I wonder if I should. Fantasy has a reputation of being cliché and derivative and generally about nondescript fantasy kingdoms with inexplicable magic. Most days I think that reputation is monstrously unfair because there's so much innovation and complexity in the genre. Other days I fall across books like this, which aren't bad, specifically, they're just ... nothing special. Probably the vast majority of fantasy is like this, but I'm really good at picking outstanding books so I tend to forget about these others. I find these disappointing because it wouldn't take much to elevate it from "standard" to "good" or even interesting. One outstanding character. A quirky detail in the setting. Prose that oozes personality. They're not too hard to achieve, and they make books memorable.<br /><br />Anyway, I think this would be a reasonable book for an older child who cannot be stopped from consuming every book in the vicinity and just needs more reading material. Otherwise, there are plenty of books that do everything better than this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8255683004096682571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/162759-margaret">Margaret</a>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780823415328" href="/book/show/1443570.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=fantasy-and-science-fiction">fantasy-and-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=children-s-and-ya-fiction">children-s-and-ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=authors-gh">authors-gh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100526210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15749216590786712536">Princess Torina is the seer, who glimpses visions in a crystal given to her by her father, the king of Archeld, who wrested it from the conquered kingdom of Bellandra. Along with the crystal, the king took Bellandra's legendary sword and hid it -- but he also took the prince of Bellandra, Landen, who longs to recover the sword and his kingdom. Eventually, Torina's fate is woven with Landen's, as her kingdom is endangered as well and they must turn to the high king, Dahmis of Glavenrell, for help</span>
  <span id="freeText15749216590786712536" style="display:none">Princess Torina is the seer, who glimpses visions in a crystal given to her by her father, the king of Archeld, who wrested it from the conquered kingdom of Bellandra. Along with the crystal, the king took Bellandra's legendary sword and hid it -- but he also took the prince of Bellandra, Landen, who longs to recover the sword and his kingdom. Eventually, Torina's fate is woven with Landen's, as her kingdom is endangered as well and they must turn to the high king, Dahmis of Glavenrell, for help.<br /><br />Unfortunately, for a story that's full of political intrigue, the worldbuilding isn't quite deep enough to sustain interest; the many kingdoms are sketchily detailed, and there's little sense of their history or culture, which makes the interactions between them less compelling than it should be. On the plus side, Hanley has created several very engaging characters -- the bold Torina and the thoughtful Landen are an interesting couple, as she learns wisdom through the crystal and he learns to take action, and many of the supporting characters are nicely sketched out as well. <br /><br />This is Hanley's first novel, and she's written at least one more in the same world; <i>The Seer and the Sword</i> was promising enough that I'll seek out the second book in the hopes of a little more worldbuilding and the same good characterization. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15749216590786712536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123953974" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123953974" />
    <a title="Maureen E" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/984514-maureen-e"><img alt="Maureen E" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528413241p2/984514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123953974?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen E" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen E" href="/user/show/984514-maureen-e">Maureen E</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984514-maureen-e?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984514-maureen-e?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123953974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13200804894884665712">by Victoria Hanley<br/><br/>Opening line--"In the castle of Archeld, Queen Dreea sat at her loom."<br/><br/>Sometimes I go through Amazon's recommendations page, just to see what they think I would like. Every so often something catches my eye and I put it on the TBR list. That was the case with this one. <a href='http://bysinginglight.files.wordpress.com/2010/09/n25372.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339990i/696549.jpg' alt='' width='143' height='237' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>From the front flap: "Princess Torina lives a charmed life in the kingdom of Archeld. Then her father, King Kareed, seizes the peaceful kingdom of Bellandra--and its legendary sword, rumored able to defeat any</span>
  <span id="freeText13200804894884665712" style="display:none">by Victoria Hanley<br><br>Opening line--"In the castle of Archeld, Queen Dreea sat at her loom."<br><br>Sometimes I go through Amazon's recommendations page, just to see what they think I would like. Every so often something catches my eye and I put it on the TBR list. That was the case with this one. <a href="http://bysinginglight.files.wordpress.com/2010/09/n25372.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339990i/696549.jpg" alt="" width="143" height="237" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>From the front flap: "Princess Torina lives a charmed life in the kingdom of Archeld. Then her father, King Kareed, seizes the peaceful kingdom of Bellandra--and its legendary sword, rumored able to defeat any enemy. On his return he offers Torina two gifts: a beautiful crystal and the defeated king's son, Landen, as a slave."<br><br>Overall, I felt like Hanley took what could have been a fairly stereotypical fantasy and somehow made it feel like it had integrity. There were some very interesting and nuanced characters, as well as a pretty standard baddie. I did feel like I never got a real sense of what distinguished the different countries. Oh, sure, Archeld is warlike while Bellandra is full of art and peace. But what about the smaller, everyday things--language and food and dress? I do really wish that authors would think about these things more often. Still, despite a couple of eye-roll moments (of <em>course</em> Torina has red hair and green eyes), the story felt engaging.<br><br>I did notice some fairly clunky writing, however, which definitely pulled me out of the flow. I'm not finding a specific example at the moment and I think it did even out as the book progressed. PW says it's for ages 12 up, and I felt like it was in some ways because Hanley was trying to write for a younger audience and wasn't quite sure how to do it. Just as a final note--there is a LOT of death in this book, more than I would have expected for that age group.<br><br>Book source: public library<br>Book information: Holiday House, 2000</span>
  <a data-text-id="13200804894884665712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73946263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73946263" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73946263?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73946263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1638199364409245119">Woo, I finished this. Here’s another sweet, traditional, straight-up fantasy for the young adult audiences. The characters are a bit one dimensional but that doesn’t make them less likable because they were easy to get along with and didn’t have any overly annoying vices that made you want to rip your hair out. <br/><br/>A lot of the story’s plot or make up of it uses a lot of clichés but as they say, it’s how you write them that counts the most. And Victoria Hanley’s writing, while rough around the edges</span>
  <span id="freeText1638199364409245119" style="display:none">Woo, I finished this. Here’s another sweet, traditional, straight-up fantasy for the young adult audiences. The characters are a bit one dimensional but that doesn’t make them less likable because they were easy to get along with and didn’t have any overly annoying vices that made you want to rip your hair out. <br /><br />A lot of the story’s plot or make up of it uses a lot of clichés but as they say, it’s how you write them that counts the most. And Victoria Hanley’s writing, while rough around the edges, is quick and snappy, dealing out pretty descriptions that make her world come to life. In the beginning it was quite a slow read, but as the plot unfolds, it begins to grab your interest with more and more ferocity. <br /><br />The big part of the hook came when we are introduced to another character, which I’m sure was not meant to be thought of as a rival for Princess Torina’s affections, but I spun a love triangle out of them anyway. Then the big woosh to the end had me riveted. The battle was fantastic, well thought out, and swift. It didn’t drag on too long, nor did it become overly redundant.<br /><br />For the most part, there isn’t a lot of violence/blood shed in this book, so it’s okay to read for the younger teens. A nice read but nothing deep or unique brought to the genre. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1638199364409245119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer36511434" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7215515612805589397">I read this book a while ago, but I loved it so much I still enjoy rereading it. The main protagonist is Torina, a rebellious young girl whose father is a conquerer of land. Upon conquering the peaceful neighboring country of Bellandra, he gives his daughter two presents which both turn out to be more precious than anything: a round crystal, in which she sees the future, and the ex-prince, Landen, as a slave. Torina instantly frees Landen, who is having trouble adjusting to living under the rule</span>
  <span id="freeText7215515612805589397" style="display:none">I read this book a while ago, but I loved it so much I still enjoy rereading it. The main protagonist is Torina, a rebellious young girl whose father is a conquerer of land. Upon conquering the peaceful neighboring country of Bellandra, he gives his daughter two presents which both turn out to be more precious than anything: a round crystal, in which she sees the future, and the ex-prince, Landen, as a slave. Torina instantly frees Landen, who is having trouble adjusting to living under the rule of his father's murderer. Though Torina and Landen form a bond of friendship, circumstance cools that over the years. When a plot is revealed to kill Torina's father, Landen flees, worried he will become the main suspect. Torina witnesses her father's death and escapes his murderer's clutches. While Landen forms a name for himself, Torina learns what it's like to not be a princess. Seperately, they both work with the high king for peace among the countries. This book is such a wonderful combination of action, romance, humor and drama that there is no chance of getting bored. Seriously. Read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7215515612805589397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082237338" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11130670474893905539">Awesome. <br/>Beautiful. <br/>Thrilling. <br/>Clever. <br/><br/>I was entranced and excited. It was a WOW. <div id="review_3490042707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3490042707" />
    <a title="Maggie Shirley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8414249-maggie-shirley"><img alt="Maggie Shirley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584837355p2/8414249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3490042707?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Shirley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Shirley" href="/user/show/8414249-maggie-shirley">Maggie Shirley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439012829" href="/book/show/1443571.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8414249-maggie-shirley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3490042707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9247938674436120823">I first read this book in third or fourth grade and absolutely loved it, but I hadn’t read again until this week and IT HOLDS UP. I had only a few very vague memories of the plot, so it was like reading it for the first time and I was totally gripped by the story. All of the characters are great, but I can especially see why I loved it so much when I was little because Princess Torina is a total badass. UGH IT WAS SO GOOD.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer349157198769653303">I have read this book a few times, there is something fun about curling up and reading a book that you have read before. It’s fun to revisit favorite characters and reenter enchanting worlds. Victoria Hanley has come up with a great story with a marvelous plot, containing many twists and turns. Torina has a rare ability of a Seer, with the aid of her crystal she can see the future and past. When her evil fiancé finds out of this gift he is set on making her his slave, and taking over the kingdom</span>
  <span id="freeText349157198769653303" style="display:none">I have read this book a few times, there is something fun about curling up and reading a book that you have read before. It’s fun to revisit favorite characters and reenter enchanting worlds. Victoria Hanley has come up with a great story with a marvelous plot, containing many twists and turns. Torina has a rare ability of a Seer, with the aid of her crystal she can see the future and past. When her evil fiancé finds out of this gift he is set on making her his slave, and taking over the kingdom. With quick wit she is able to escape and goes into hiding. Meanwhile, her childhood friend Landen also goes on the run for being falsely accused of killing Torina’s father, King Kareed. The majority of the book they are separated during their journeys. Usually I hate this in books, but for some reason in this book it is done so well and each character undergoes so much that when they are finally reunited they are better people and it is a sweet reunion. I love this book, it is one of my favorites and I recommend that everyone read it. It contains everything you want in a great book.     <a title="Sonja P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4724912-sonja-p"><img alt="Sonja P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519007692p2/4724912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261028275?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonja P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja P." href="/user/show/4724912-sonja-p">Sonja P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4724912-sonja-p?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261028275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13710833308867792547">Where did I get this book?: I got it from a used book store. It looked interesting, so I went for it.<br/><br/>Plot: Torina is granted two gifts when her father comes back from war one day: a crystal and a slave boy named Landen. Landen is the prince of the kingdom her father has defeated, and Torina immediately frees and befriends him. She also discovers she can see the future in the crystal she carries. Years pass, and suddenly people are saying Landen is going to kill her father. How can she defend her</span>
  <span id="freeText13710833308867792547" style="display:none">Where did I get this book?: I got it from a used book store. It looked interesting, so I went for it.<br /><br />Plot: Torina is granted two gifts when her father comes back from war one day: a crystal and a slave boy named Landen. Landen is the prince of the kingdom her father has defeated, and Torina immediately frees and befriends him. She also discovers she can see the future in the crystal she carries. Years pass, and suddenly people are saying Landen is going to kill her father. How can she defend her kingdom, and decide who to trust?<br /><br />Negatives: This book is definitely written for children, so be prepared for some simplistic writing and plot details. I also didn’t like that Torina seemed sidelined a lot in favor of Landen. She was often painted as a helpless female which was a little infuriating. She grew out of this a bit, but I would have liked to have seen her be more active. Parts of the book also seemed to happen really quickly, but again, this could be contributed to it being aimed at a younger audience.<br /><br />Positives: I really loved Landen, and I thought the story as a whole was really captivating and enjoyable. I think Hanley developed her plot, and really made it exciting. I like that Landen went in a different direction than I expected, and I think that Torina being able to tell the future worked really well in certain parts of the story. It was nice just to read a simple story for once without a lot of angst or triangles. <br /><br />Rating: 3 out of 5 Crystals<br /><br />Recommend: I would definitely recommend this for younger readers, and if you like fantasy, I would give it a shot as its a relatively quick, entertaining read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13710833308867792547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780823415328" href="/book/show/1443570.The_Seer_and_the_Sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805250469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3632770631813393027">Princess Torina's father conquers the peaceful kingdom of Bellandra and takes with him two presents for her: a seer crystal and the Bellandran prince to be her slave. Torina immediately frees the prince, Landen, who becomes her friend and archery-tutor. When the chief adviser murders the king and tries to marry Torina, Torina's skill with the seer crystal and Landen's loyalty keep her relatively safe. Torina and Landen flee the kingdom on opposite trajectories: Landen becomes the leader of a sor</span>
  <span id="freeText3632770631813393027" style="display:none">Princess Torina's father conquers the peaceful kingdom of Bellandra and takes with him two presents for her: a seer crystal and the Bellandran prince to be her slave. Torina immediately frees the prince, Landen, who becomes her friend and archery-tutor. When the chief adviser murders the king and tries to marry Torina, Torina's skill with the seer crystal and Landen's loyalty keep her relatively safe. Torina and Landen flee the kingdom on opposite trajectories: Landen becomes the leader of a sort of state-sponsored band of Merry Men, while Torina makes a quiet life for herself in the country. Eventually, prompted by their consciences, both Torina and Landen independently seek to help the High King against treachery and invasion. In so doing they not only save many kingdoms, but they also find each other once more.<br /><br />A sweet tale, but I was frustrated by how resistant Landen and Torina were to revealing their true identities. Long after they should have told the High King who they were, each of them remained obstinately silent; a good portion of the Vesputo's plots would have been prevented if either (or both!) of them had revealed themselves. The book is plagued with annoyances like that, and by a distressing choice to repeatedly skip over very interesting sections of Torina and Landen's lives with just a quick summary. Landen leads an entire band of former thieves that once tried to kill him in gladiatorial games! That should get us at least a paragraph or two, instead of a quick mention of it! Anyway, it's overall a fine adventure with a nice anti-war message, and it was a good enough yarn that I read it in a single evening rather than put it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3632770631813393027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_295980742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295980742" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7272476-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295980742?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/7272476-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295980742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7141350097290886588">I've read this story many times and each time I am reminded just how much I love this book. I like books that make me feel something. Whether it makes me happy or sad or angry, if it makes me feel something, I have a stronger reaction to the story. Bonus if the story makes me feel all of the above. And this story always does. There are times while reading this story that I am just so angry that I want to throw the book across the room and be done but I love he story too much for that. <br/><br/>At the beg</span>
  <span id="freeText7141350097290886588" style="display:none">I've read this story many times and each time I am reminded just how much I love this book. I like books that make me feel something. Whether it makes me happy or sad or angry, if it makes me feel something, I have a stronger reaction to the story. Bonus if the story makes me feel all of the above. And this story always does. There are times while reading this story that I am just so angry that I want to throw the book across the room and be done but I love he story too much for that. <br /><br />At the beginning of the book, Torina is a young, spoiled princess who is given two presents from her father King Kareed; a crystal, which she soon discovers shows her the future, and a young boy to be her slave, who she quickly sets free and who becomes her best friend. The young boy was the prince of the country that Kareed had just conquered. The story follows their lives as they deal with exile and war and separation. They each go their separate ways but their lives mirror each other. <br /><br />I love the interaction between Torina and Landen. I love how strong and fiery Torina is and how strong and noble Landen is. The characters are what makes the story for me. Every character in the story, you get to know and like for what they are. Even the antagonists are deliciously evil.<br /><br />Definitely a story that will always be a favorite. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7141350097290886588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_26828130" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26828130" />
    <a title="Tortla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95618-tortla"><img alt="Tortla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251327418p2/95618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26828130?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tortla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tortla" href="/user/show/95618-tortla">Tortla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618-tortla?shelf=dragons-and-fantasy">dragons-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618-tortla?shelf=feministy">feministy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618-tortla?shelf=multiple-perspectives">multiple-perspectives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618-tortla?shelf=ya-like">ya-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26828130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16683487653652108544">The name "Torina" is silly. Also, this book read rather like a movie, what with its chapter-endings and perspective-switches. In spite of this, The Seer and the Sword remains interesting and unique enough to be redeemed...a little. I'm still rather irked by its very un-subtle (and quite convenient) romance, as well as the cheesy character-growth near the end.<br/>The story was interesting, but probably suffered from its distractingly contrived writing. I'm pretty sure the phrase "hooked up" was used,</span>
  <span id="freeText16683487653652108544" style="display:none">The name "Torina" is silly. Also, this book read rather like a movie, what with its chapter-endings and perspective-switches. In spite of this, The Seer and the Sword remains interesting and unique enough to be redeemed...a little. I'm still rather irked by its very un-subtle (and quite convenient) romance, as well as the cheesy character-growth near the end.<br />The story was interesting, but probably suffered from its distractingly contrived writing. I'm pretty sure the phrase "hooked up" was used, in reference to two characters being reunited. I'm not sure if it was an attempt to relate to the YA-audience or if it was just the author's (kind of bad) style. Also, the "good guys" were way too noble and the "bad guys" were practically inhuman. Realistic characterization would be kind of nice.<br />I guess this book is a good read if you're really bored or desperate for something to read, but if you want to read a YA fantasy book with a strong female heroine I vote for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/407813.The_Blue_Sword__Damar___1_" title="The Blue Sword (Damar, #1) by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Blue Sword</a>...Better written and still largely about a sword. And (if I remember correctly) I'm pretty sure that The Blue Sword's heroine is a redhead, too. Whose name is far superior to "Torina."</span>
  <a data-text-id="16683487653652108544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1502413274" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1502413274" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1136088-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1502413274?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/1136088-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1136088-grace?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1136088-grace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1136088-grace?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1502413274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15967617789812054043">Disappointing.<br/><br/>I had eyed this book for a long time before picking it up and then it was good, right up until they grew up, which was far in the beginning of the book. To be fair, the setup for the story was interesting, in Landen's family being a cultured, knowledge-based society, and Torina's father being first and foremost a (barbarian) conqueror. Landen had to really prove himself to be accepted into the society that conquered him and took him as prisoner of war.<br/><br/>I found the viewpoint of Lande</span>
  <span id="freeText15967617789812054043" style="display:none">Disappointing.<br /><br />I had eyed this book for a long time before picking it up and then it was good, right up until they grew up, which was far in the beginning of the book. To be fair, the setup for the story was interesting, in Landen's family being a cultured, knowledge-based society, and Torina's father being first and foremost a (barbarian) conqueror. Landen had to really prove himself to be accepted into the society that conquered him and took him as prisoner of war.<br /><br />I found the viewpoint of Landen to be sort of girly and unconvincing. He's the one pining for Torina long after they are no longer friends. He moons after her from afar, and it just seemed...fake. He's a young boy, with his own problems and friends, and yet during the years they grew apart and Torina starts getting a crush on someone else (the one trying to kill her father), he's basically stalking her. And not in a touching way. Sort of like a teenage fantasy emo-boy way. Which I guess he sort of is.<br /><br />Meh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15967617789812054043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_188218317" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188218317" />
    <a title="Kiersten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten"><img alt="Kiersten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323835889p2/5861997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188218317?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiersten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiersten" href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten">Kiersten</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188218317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16504620152657556365">This was way better than i was expecting it to be. I went into this expecting a somewhat watery, hackneyed plot line with a few good twists and characters if I was lucky, but I found myself completely hooked as soon as I started reading. Although it's still definitely not the most original story ever, Hanley's writing style and vibrant characters make the story come alive. The backstory was well-developed, and the main plot and the characters' behavior were consistent with it. Almost all the cha</span>
  <span id="freeText16504620152657556365" style="display:none">This was way better than i was expecting it to be. I went into this expecting a somewhat watery, hackneyed plot line with a few good twists and characters if I was lucky, but I found myself completely hooked as soon as I started reading. Although it's still definitely not the most original story ever, Hanley's writing style and vibrant characters make the story come alive. The backstory was well-developed, and the main plot and the characters' behavior were consistent with it. Almost all the characters were dynamic, changing and growing over the course of the story, and the changing point of view was unusually believable. I found it to be a suspenseful and emotional book, and not too slow, even though the story spans ten years. The ending was really sweet. A cute love story, but still packed with action and intrigue, and dark enough to be plausible. This was a really solid, memorable fantasy tale, and I'll probably check out some of Victoria Hanley's other books. I loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16504620152657556365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r5wkGw1iaq+Med2a8+41aAHhgDrVKYqfPgVrqMHA5Kcg197LxOM70d/y5MRxqxg1cOv0jOkavGJqsXd8o+CJtg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HmQIYMU2Fi4o4qyl5MM+LShdDEdtbcZsAeHJUCk1xNmRL/KwDLdHUHtplftmhhNwWVd48VFe8JFVVdWESxWpyA==')})
  }
//]]>
